    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1712822778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712822778" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729639-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579967825p2/4729639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712822778?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/4729639-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345810427" href="/book/show/27876415-do-not-say-we-have-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=can-con">can-con</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=man-booker-nod">man-booker-nod</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712822778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10122020987854008161"><blockquote><i>“Jiang Kai,” she said spitefully, “now I understand. I'll forget Prokofiev. I'll play the 'March of the Volunteers' and 'The Internationale' for all eternity. </i>The old world shall be destroyed. Arise, slaves, arise! Do not say that we have nothing.<i> That should win me the Tchaikovsky Competition and please everyone, you most of all.”</i></blockquote><br/>I remember having read <a href='http://news.nationalpost.com/full-comment/jonathan-kay-twenty-five-years-later-our-democratic-reveries-about-tiananmen-square-seem-ridiculous' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> article on the 25th anniversary of the Tiananmen Square protests (back in 2014), and the point that impressed upon me most of all is that t</span>
  <span id="freeText10122020987854008161" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>“Jiang Kai,” she said spitefully, “now I understand. I'll forget Prokofiev. I'll play the 'March of the Volunteers' and 'The Internationale' for all eternity. </i>The old world shall be destroyed. Arise, slaves, arise! Do not say that we have nothing.<i> That should win me the Tchaikovsky Competition and please everyone, you most of all.”</i></blockquote><br />I remember having read <a href="http://news.nationalpost.com/full-comment/jonathan-kay-twenty-five-years-later-our-democratic-reveries-about-tiananmen-square-seem-ridiculous" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> article on the 25th anniversary of the Tiananmen Square protests (back in 2014), and the point that impressed upon me most of all is that the young Chinese students of today's Beijing – with their smart phones and consumer goods and upwardly mobile prospects – have no awareness of the near grasp of democracy that happened scant years before their births; indeed, of the one hundred random students shown the famous “Tank Man” picture, only nineteen knew what it represented, and of them, no one was comfortable talking about it. It's <i>nearly</i> comprehensible that a dictatorship like the Chinese government could erase all public acknowledgement of Tiananmen and the massacre that happened there, but what about word of mouth? Have the witnesses from that day <i>never</i> told the story to their children, behind closed doors, in hushed whispers? In the narrative laid out by Madeleine Thien in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27876415.Do_Not_Say_We_Have_Nothing" title="Do Not Say We Have Nothing by Madeleine Thien" rel="nofollow noopener">Do Not Say We Have Nothing</a>, this is exactly what happens: official and private silence has been the routine response to the various tragedies suffered by the Chinese people throughout the twentieth century. In Thien's hands, this makes for a fascinating story.<br /><br />As the book opens, it is 1989 Vancouver, and ten-year-old Chinese-Canadian Marie is mourning her father's sudden disappearance and suicide earlier in the year. Soon, a relative of sorts, Ai-ming, comes from Beijing to stay with Marie and her mother, and when Ai-ming discovers a chapter of a hand-written novel (known as the <i>Book of Records</i>) among Marie's father's notebooks, she is able to explain its history and recite the rest of the known chapters to Marie from memory. As it turns out, the <i>Book of Records</i> was an incomplete <i>samizdat</i>-type document that Ai-ming's great uncle, Wen the Dreamer, had used to court her great aunt Swirl, and when they were later separated during the Cultural Revolution, each of them created further copies of the novel, inserting small variations in the Chinese characters in order to communicate with one another. After Wen escaped from a remote prison camp and reunited with Swirl, he determined to preserve the names of those who had died in prison by continuing the story of the still unfinished <i>Book of Records</i>:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>He would populate this fictional world with true names and true deeds. They would live on, as dangerous as revolutionaries but as intangible as ghosts. What new movement could the Party proclaim that would bring these dead souls into line? What crackdown could erase something that was hidden in plain sight?</blockquote>
</i><br />Each chapter of <i>Do Not Say We Have Nothing</i> starts from Marie's perspective – in either her “present” of 1989/90, when she is learning from Ai-ming, or her “present” of 2016, when she is searching China and the internet for the now-missing Ai-ming – and through all of the time-hopping and Ai-ming's storytelling, the reader is eventually filled in on the three generations of Ai-ming's family that span the post-WWII years: Swirl and Wen the Dreamer who, as minor figures in a family of landowners, are attacked and sent for re-education (during Mao's years of land reformation) by the angry mob that used to be their friends and neighbours; their daughter Zhuli (a violinist) and her cousin Sparrow (a composer and Ai-ming's father) who were attacked by their former friends and colleagues (now Red Guards) at the Shanghai Conservatory of Music during the Cultural Revolution; and Ai-ming's participation in the student protests at Tiananmen Square (and the consequences of that participation that prompted her to flee China). In every one of these violent government-sponsored crackdowns, it's the people who join the mob who seem to escape punishment; and those who cannot join do well to remain silent. Throughout it all, while the citizens may rightly fear for their own lives, they actually believe in the Revolution; understand that the few must be sacrificed in order to secure the happiness and prosperity of the many; little wonder that they who witnessed the massacre at Tiananmen would protect the next generation from the knowledge that protest is even possible.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>I assumed that when the story finished, life would continue and I would go back to being myself. But it wasn't true. The stories got longer and longer, and I got smaller and smaller. When I told Big Mother this, she laughed her head off. “But that's how the world is, isn't it?”</blockquote>
</i><br />That is a very bare bones outline of the plot, but this book is <i>dense</i> with history and ideas. It's also one of those books about musicians where the musically uneducated reader is at a definite disadvantage: I'm sure I would have identified more with the characters if I knew the physical <i>need</i> to perform certain music or the intimate process of composition; if I could tell the difference between Bach and Shostakovitch. This book has funny passages, and touching passages, and devastating passages. I loved the framing device of the <i>Book of Records</i>: initially discovered by Wen the Dreamer, he recognised that variations in hand-drawn Chinese characters between editions probably meant it was being used for secret communication ---&gt; this leads to Wen and Swirl using the book in the same manner to communicate with one another; now aided by the use of a mimeograph machine ---&gt; this leads to Marie trying to communicate with the lost Ai-ming by digitally leaving the book around the world; now aided by the use of the internet: despite generations of government censors trying to purge the Chinese citizens of individual thought, this little novel remains beneath the radar; and despite the fact that those censors are still at work today, this book seems like an important continuation of the (fictional) <i>Book of Records</i> itself. <br /><br />Here's the bottom line: there is much to like about <i>Do Not Say We Have Nothing</i>, but in the end, I respected it more than I enjoyed it; it feels <i>important</i>, if not totally accessible. I have no doubt that it will make more awards lists (it was recently longlisted for the 2016 Man Booker Prize), but ultimately, I got the sense that Thien was writing more for her peers in the literary community than for the general reading public. Even so, what she has created bears witness to decades of what the Chinese government has suppressed: it <u>needed</u> to be written and I can't deny that it represents a worthy achievement.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10122020987854008161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756858352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756858352" />
    <a title="Maria Hill AKA MH Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books"><img alt="Maria Hill AKA MH Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566664384p2/46346297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756858352?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Hill AKA MH Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Hill AKA MH Books" href="/user/show/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books">Maria Hill AKA MH Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781783782666" href="/book/show/30037751-do-not-say-we-have-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=want-to-read-again">want-to-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=china">china</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=canada">canada</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46346297-maria-hill-aka-mh-books?shelf=books-i-own-and-have-read">books-i-own-and-have-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756858352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1642886947461735860">This book demands to be read slowly, perhaps best summarised by a single sentence in chapter 2.<br/><br/>“And even when I answered him in my impeccable Canadian accent, he continued with the slowness of the ages, until I, too, felt my pulse slow, and time became relative, as the physicists have proved it was, so perhaps Ai-Ming and I are still seated there, in a corner of the restaurant, waiting for our meal to come, for a sentence to end, for this intermission to run its course.”<br/><br/><br/>The book is an epic story</span>
  <span id="freeText1642886947461735860" style="display:none">This book demands to be read slowly, perhaps best summarised by a single sentence in chapter 2.<br /><br />“And even when I answered him in my impeccable Canadian accent, he continued with the slowness of the ages, until I, too, felt my pulse slow, and time became relative, as the physicists have proved it was, so perhaps Ai-Ming and I are still seated there, in a corner of the restaurant, waiting for our meal to come, for a sentence to end, for this intermission to run its course.”<br /><br /><br />The book is an epic story of China over 60 years from Mao's Cultural Revolution to the Student protest in Tiananmen Square in 1989 (which I barely remember as images of tanks on the news). The story revolves around three classical musicians and their families; Sparrow (Bird of Quiet), a composer, Kai a pianist and Zhuli a violinist. Music and its affects are therefore central to the thinking, behaviours and motives of the characters. I don’t know much about classical music but playing some of the mentioned pieces on Spotify while reading the book certainly helped my understanding here. Thien takes these passionate characters and pitches them against the constraints of communism, the Cultural Revolution and ultimately the rise and fall of the peoples hopes for change at Tiananmen Square. Every character is searching for (and sometimes loosing) their own identity amongst the chaos "I've been searching for myself but I didn't expect to find so many selves of mine.”<br /><br /><br />There are also intriguing mentions of the Chinese languages, the multiple meanings of its characters and how writing (even hateful writing) can be beautiful and tell you something of the author. The importance of writing can be found in protest signs, musical notation, the hand-copied Book of Records (an epic novel within this epic novel) and in self-criticisms (that citizens are forced to write).<br /><br /><br />Personally, this book has opened up an understanding to me of the Chinese women I worked with while studying for my PhD in the UK. They too had arrived there on international scholarships and I think finally I understand something of what they were trying to tell me. For this I thank Thien and of course them. <br /><br />I will <br />be reading this book again and it is my favourite for the Man Booker prize - though I still have to read Hot Milk.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1642886947461735860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2470429636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2470429636" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2470429636?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345810427" href="/book/show/27876415-do-not-say-we-have-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=canadian-content">canadian-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2470429636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2027168094170368260">A fabulously written story of three generations of family and friends living through the tumult of the Cultural Revolution and then the political upheaval culminating in the Tiananmen Square demonstrations. <br/><br/>This is fiction based on reality, and in so many ways it reads like the most frightening of dystopias. But at it's heart is the story of the many ways people choose to survive, or not, in the times and circumstances they have been born into.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2387897504" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2387897504" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8051792-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544530609p2/8051792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2387897504?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/8051792-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387897504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7546351119171259911">This was not one of those satisfying historical novels that I was able to curl up with and get lost in. I struggled with it - especially the first half. The characters are frustratingly elusive. But perhaps that is the point? Thien doesn't make it easy to attach to them. <br/><br/>Music is central to the novel and the driving force for Zhuli, Sparrow and Kai. At times, the discussion of specific compositions went overboard and felt like name-dropping to me. Thien flooded the pages with the names of compos</span>
  <span id="freeText7546351119171259911" style="display:none">This was not one of those satisfying historical novels that I was able to curl up with and get lost in. I struggled with it - especially the first half. The characters are frustratingly elusive. But perhaps that is the point? Thien doesn't make it easy to attach to them. <br /><br />Music is central to the novel and the driving force for Zhuli, Sparrow and Kai. At times, the discussion of specific compositions went overboard and felt like name-dropping to me. Thien flooded the pages with the names of composers and musical pieces. I did find a playlist on Spotify with most of the music mentioned: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://open.spotify.com/user/theamericanscholar/playlist/6WvLaEX8B7HoJpYkBNt0BA">https://open.spotify.com/user/theamer...</a><br /><br />In spite of these criticisms, I really liked this novel! Thien brilliantly captures the shifting political terrain in China from the 1950s to the 1989 Tiananmen Square protests. By the last third, I couldn't put it down. It didn't deliver what I thought I wanted, but instead gave me something more profound.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7546351119171259911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GWk6I06ocJv1kWuSei78UMHpDgEcE/sQWzSNzGHzllN5l0NqCM1p0skydpdXL12MpScWJZpKxU8hAVrrGCgY9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i3mOcUWtaqfbmM6YkR/Jj6voYyKQAp5fTWrYi0dDWRHrh/c4A8hz7uc70528HmhTzyZ7BhZboAA3Xw+sPpjXtA==')})
  }

Eventually the children landed in the home of their paternal grandparents, but their tough-love attitudes meant conflicts became commonplace. And the ghost of Jesse’s drug-addicted father haunted the halls of the house and the memories of every family member. One day, he finally realized he would die unless he turned his life around.In this heartwarming and heartbreaking memoir, Jesse Thistle writes honestly and fearlessly about his painful experiences with abuse, uncovering the truth about his parents, and how he found his way back into the circle of his Indigenous culture and family through education.An eloquent exploration of what it means to The exciting first novel in her trickster trilogy.\n\nEveryone knows a guy like Jared: the burnout kid in high school who sells weed cookies and has a scary mom who\'s often wasted and wielding some kind of weapon. Jared does smoke and drink too much, and he does make the best cookies in town, and his mom is a mess, but he\'s also a kid who has an immense capacity for compassion and an impulse to watch over people more than twice his age, and he can\'t rely on anyone for consistent love and support, except for his flatulent pit bull, Baby Killer (he calls her Baby)--and now she\'s dead. \n\nJared can\'t count on his mom to stay sober and stick around to take care of him. He can\'t rely on his dad to pay the bills and support his new wife and step-daughter. Jared is only sixteen but feels like he is the one who must stabilize his family\'s life, even look out for his elderly neighbours. But he struggles to keep everything afloat...and sometimes he blacks out. And he puzzles over why his maternal grandmother has never liked him, why she says he\'s the son of a trickster, that he isn\'t human. Each of them at a different stage in life, each of them away from home, and each of them striving -- in the suburbs of Prague, in an overdeveloped Alpine village, beside a Belgian motorway, in a dingy Cyprus hotel -- to understand what it m<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText746546721772076058\" style=\"display:none\">Nine men. Each of them at a different stage in life, each of them away from home, and each of them striving -- in the suburbs of Prague, in an overdeveloped Alpine village, beside a Belgian motorway, in a dingy Cyprus hotel -- to understand what it means to be alive, here and now. Tracing a dramatic arc from the spring of youth to the winter of old age, the ostensibly separate narratives of All That Man Is aggregate into a picture of a single shared existence, a picture that interrogates the state of modern manhood while bringing to life, unforgettably, the physical and emotional terrain of an increasingly globalized Europe. And so these nine lives form an ingenious and new kind of novel, in which David Szalay expertly plots a dark predicament for the twenty-first-century man.\n\nDark and disturbing, but also often wickedly and uproariously comic, All That Man Is is notable for the acute psychological penetration Szalay brings to bear on his characters, from the working-class ex-grunt to the pompous college student, the middle-aged loser to the Russian oligarch. Steadily and mercilessly, as this brilliantly conceived book progresses, the protagonist at the center of each chapter is older than the last one, it gets colder out, and All That Man Is gathers exquisite power. Szalay is a writer of supreme gifts -- a master of a new kind of realism that vibrates with detail, intelligence, relevance, and devastating pathos.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"746546721772076058\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/265535.Madeleine_Thien">About Madeleine Thien</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/265535.Madeleine_Thien"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1451969480p3/265535.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/265535.Madeleine_Thien">Madeleine Thien
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
518
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12880011204346636328">Madeleine Thien was born in Vancouver. She is the author of the story collection <em>Simple Recipes</em> (2001), and three novels, <em>Certainty</em> (2006); <em>Dogs at the Perimeter</em> (2011), shortlisted for Berlin’s International Literature Prize and winner of the Frankfurt Book Fair’s 2015 Liberaturpreis; and <em>Do Not Say We Have Nothing</em> (2016), about musicians studying Western classical music at the Shanghai Conservat</span>
  <span id="freeText12880011204346636328" style="display:none">Madeleine Thien was born in Vancouver. She is the author of the story collection <em>Simple Recipes</em> (2001), and three novels, <em>Certainty</em> (2006); <em>Dogs at the Perimeter</em> (2011), shortlisted for Berlin’s International Literature Prize and winner of the Frankfurt Book Fair’s 2015 Liberaturpreis; and <em>Do Not Say We Have Nothing</em> (2016), about musicians studying Western classical music at the Shanghai Conservatory in the 1960s, and about the legacy of the 1989 Tiananmen demonstrations. Her books and stories are published in Canada, the U.S., the U.K. and Australia, and have been translated into 25 languages. <br /><br /><em>Do Not Say We Have Nothing</em> won the 2016 Scotiabank Giller Prize, the 2016 Governor-General’s Literary Award for Fiction, and an Edward Stanford Prize; and was shortlisted for the 2016 Man Booker Prize, the 2017 Baileys Women’s Prize for Fiction, and The Folio Prize 2017. The novel was named a <em>New York Times</em> Critics’ Top Book of 2016 and longlisted for a Carnegie Medal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12880011204346636328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
